*     [![ArtRabbit App in situ, map view, 2025. Heat map of exhibitions across New York; tapping on a cluster reveals precise location pins and detailed information for each event. Photograph by Tom Elsner. Courtesy ArtRabbit.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/the-new-york-times-named-artrabbit-a-leading-art-discovery-platform-heres-why-that-matters/image/images/VTLJavsYhqYX/345x460/0,0/1700x2264/artrabbit-app-1.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/the-new-york-times-named-artrabbit-a-leading-art-discovery-platform-heres-why-that-matters/image/images/hDB3q3fG7qZr/690x920/0,0/1700x2264/artrabbit-app-1.jpg)

*     [![ArtRabbit App in situ, event detail page, 2025. Carousel of exhibition images alongside contextual information about the exhibition’s themes, artists, and venue, as well as visitor details like location and tickets. Photograph by Tom Elsner. Courtesy Ar](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/the-new-york-times-named-artrabbit-a-leading-art-discovery-platform-heres-why-that-matters/image/images/5XCtjiMYmxq1/343x460/0,0/3014x4032/ArtRabbit-App-in-situ-event-detail-page-2025-Photograph-by-Tom-Elsner-Courtesy-ArtRabbit.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/the-new-york-times-named-artrabbit-a-leading-art-discovery-platform-heres-why-that-matters/image/images/flYfToLqRkRZ/687x920/0,0/3014x4032/ArtRabbit-App-in-situ-event-detail-page-2025-Photograph-by-Tom-Elsner-Courtesy-ArtRabbit.jpg)
    
    **ArtRabbit App in situ, event detail page, 2025.** Carousel of exhibition images alongside contextual information about the exhibition’s themes, artists, and venue, as well as visitor details like location and tickets. Photograph by Tom Elsner. _Courtesy ArtRabbit._
    

The arts rely on real systems – digital tools, audiences, and networks – not myth. As the sector faces fragmentation, dependable infrastructure is essential. This piece explores what cultural organizations and audiences need now.

Last night I attended an off-Broadway play about two adults trying to “make painting work,” and it underscored a familiar truth. The narrative reflected a widespread belief that art exists apart from real systems, as if creative work can succeed on sincerity alone. In reality, art depends on the same structures that sustain any field: labor, economics, education, audiences, and networks. Although the arts contributed $1.2 trillion to the U.S. economy in 2023, representing 4.2 percent of national GDP, the sector remains misunderstood and fragmented.\* These gaps limit engagement, weaken visual literacy, and obstruct long-term cultural growth. \[[Read on](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/the-new-york-times-named-artrabbit-a-leading-art-discovery-platform-heres-why-that-matters)\
\]

ArtRabbit was created to help address this need.

This week, [the New York Times identified ArtRabbit as one of the leading platforms for discovering art](https://www.nytimes.com/2025/11/13/arts/design/art-influencers-apps-galleries-smartphone.html)
. The value of this recognition lies not in visibility but in the responsibility it underscores: the cultural sector requires reliable digital infrastructure. Online behavior has evolved faster than arts organizations can respond – and many platforms have failed because they lacked the systems, planning, and audience insight required for sustainable support.

Our model is designed to meet those demands.

For nearly two decades, our international team has developed a submission-based platform built on accuracy, accessibility, and long-term audience development. Through clear listings, thoughtful editorial, neighborhood pathways, curated tours, and institutional partnerships, we work to strengthen cultural participation across communities and organizations of all sizes.

We do not employ data mining or automated curation. Instead, we focus on cultivating intentional audiences that include collectors, students, researchers, arts professionals, and members of the public who rely on ArtRabbit because they trust its information and use it to guide their cultural engagement.

As AI reshapes how people search for and interpret visual material, the need for dependable and mission-aligned digital tools is increasingly urgent. Our aim is to help institutions expand their visibility, deepen public engagement, and secure a consistent presence in an increasingly crowded landscape.

Together with galleries, museums, universities, and cultural organizations, we’re continuing to build accessible and informed pathways into the arts. ArtRabbit is structured for long-term impact at the local, national, and international levels.

We welcome you to participate in what comes next, as we develop tools, partnerships, and pathways that strengthen cultural engagement. As part of this ongoing work, we’re sharing several updates on what’s happening across ArtRabbit right now:

What to see this week
---------------------

[New York](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-states/new-york)
, [London](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-kingdom/london)
, [Los Angeles](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-states/los-angeles)
, [Berlin](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/germany/berlin)
, [Singapore](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/singapore/singapore)

App Update
----------

We’ve released a new set of improvements to the ArtRabbit app. These updates include more generous visuals across the interface, faster performance, and improved map nesting to make browsing upcoming exhibitions more intuitive. We’re also developing several wishlist features shared by our community in recent weeks. Tours and more flexible landing pages are already in progress, with additional enhancements scheduled for upcoming releases.

Your feedback genuinely shapes the product, so please keep it coming. You can share it through the app or by emailing [support@artrabbit.com](mailto:support@artrabbit.com)

[Get the ArtRabbit App for iPhone or Android](https://www.artrabbit.com/about/app)

ArtRabbit’s Winter Gallery Tour in Chelsea
------------------------------------------

For our New York community, I’ll be returning in December with a special holiday edition of the ArtRabbit gallery tour, this time in Chelsea. Join us for an afternoon exploring seasonal exhibitions across the neighborhood, from Agnes Martin’s serene abstractions at Pace, to Kader Attia’s installations at Lehmann Maupin, to dynamic color-focused works at Miles McEnery Gallery. The tour features lively discussion in an intimate small-group format, followed by a complimentary glass of wine at Tia Pol.

[![ArtRabbit Winter Gallery Tour](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/artrabbit-winter-gallery-tour-2025/images/4vF43AcjiAEh/1120x1370/Lehmann-Maupin-Install.jpg)\

Art Tour\

Upcoming Miami Art Week
-----------------------

As Miami prepares for another Miami Art Week, drawing thousands of collectors, curators, and art lovers, we’re finalizing this year’s ArtRabbit Guide to Miami. If you’re an arts professional/gallery/museum, now is an ideal time to update your ArtRabbit listings with current exhibitions, extended hours, programs, or special offers for visiting audiences. If you’re traveling to Miami in December, the ArtRabbit app can help you navigate fairs, museums, and both established and emerging art spaces throughout the city.

\* Economic contribution estimates are drawn from official sources: in the United States, arts and cultural production accounted for approximately $1.17–$1.2 trillion, or 4.2% of GDP in 2023 ([U.S. Bureau of Economic Analysis, Arts & Cultural Production Satellite Account](https://www.bea.gov/news/2025/arts-and-cultural-production-satellite-account-us-and-states-2023)
). For comparison, UK creative industries generated roughly £124 billion (~5.2% of UK GVA) in 2023 ([UK Department for Culture, Media & Sport / House of Lords Library](https://lordslibrary.parliament.uk/creative-industries-growth-jobs-and-productivity/?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
). Across the European Union, cultural and creative industries contributed approximately 3.95% of EU value added ([European Commission](https://single-market-economy.ec.europa.eu/sectors/cultural-and-creative-industries_en?utm_source=chatgpt.com)
).

# New York in Miami: What Basel, NADA, and Untitled Reveal About the Year Ahead 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

*     [![Art Basel Miami Beach 2024, Lee ShinJa, Tina Kim Gallery. Courtesy of Art Basel.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/december/new-york-in-miami-what-basel-nada-and-untitled-reveal-about-the-year-ahead/image/images/krCP9lylZb4f/689x460/0,0/1439x960/Art-Basel-Miami-Art-Basel-Miami-Beach-2024-Lee-ShinJa-Tina-Kim-Gallery-Courtesy-of-Art-Basel.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/december/new-york-in-miami-what-basel-nada-and-untitled-reveal-about-the-year-ahead/image/images/N7qZ2TMCcOgi/1379x920/0,0/1439x960/Art-Basel-Miami-Art-Basel-Miami-Beach-2024-Lee-ShinJa-Tina-Kim-Gallery-Courtesy-of-Art-Basel.jpg)
    
    Art Basel Miami Beach 2024, Lee ShinJa, Tina Kim Gallery. Courtesy of Art Basel.
    
*     [![Untitled Art Miami Beach. Courtesy of Untitled Art.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/december/new-york-in-miami-what-basel-nada-and-untitled-reveal-about-the-year-ahead/image/images/O39cOg5GUUaf/691x460/0,0/3007x2000/untitled-art-fair.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/december/new-york-in-miami-what-basel-nada-and-untitled-reveal-about-the-year-ahead/image/images/fhamiHqRY01I/1383x920/0,0/3007x2000/untitled-art-fair.jpg)
    
    Untitled Art Miami Beach. Courtesy of Untitled Art.
    

New York sets the temperature for Miami Art Week, shaping the conversations that unfold across Basel, NADA, and Untitled. This guide breaks down how and where that influence appears, along with a map of every New York gallery showing in Miami.

New York will always be the center of the art world, for me. It’s the place where artists, galleries, and curators continually redefine what contemporary art can be. So while my colleagues may cast their votes for London or Hong Kong, when Miami Art Week arrives, New York doesn’t just show up, it sets the tone.

For new collectors, this can be overwhelming. There are so many fairs, so many booths, and so many stories being told at once. But once you know the character of each fair and the role New York galleries play inside them, the entire week becomes clearer, more enjoyable, and far more rewarding.

Think of the fairs as three different kinds of conversations. [Art Basel Miami Beach](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/art-basel-miami-beach-miami-beach-convention-center)
 is the one led by major museums. [NADA](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025)
 is the one led by artists and the galleries who champion them early. [Untitled Art](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/untitled-art-miami-beach)
 is the fair where materials, process, and cross disciplinary work shine.

Each fair has a very different energy and purpose. Once you understand those differences, it becomes easier to decide what you want to see and why.

Below is a welcoming, collector friendly guide to the three main fairs in Miami through the lens of New York, including four gallery highlights at each. This is written to help you walk into each fair with confidence.

[If you’re heading to Miami this week, you can read our quick guide to what’s happening across the city here.](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/december/miami-art-week-2025-what-to-see-where-to-go)

Whether you are boarding a flight this week or staying close to home, the influence of New York is impossible to miss. If you are not going to Miami, we have collated every New York gallery showing in the fairs, so you can follow the momentum from your own neighborhood and see the artists and exhibitions that anchor these Miami presentations. Scroll all the way to the end for those.

[Art Basel Miami Beach](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/art-basel-miami-beach-miami-beach)
 - The fair that reflects institutional taste and long term significance
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you want to understand what museums and major collectors are thinking about right now, Art Basel is the place to start. Basel sets the tone for the year ahead by clarifying which ideas, artists, and materials are gaining institutional momentum.

New York galleries are especially strong here. They bring scholarship, clarity, and a long view of art history. Basel is not about chasing a moment. It is about reinforcing the conversations that are shaping the field at the highest level.

[![Art Basel Miami Beach](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/art-basel-miami-beach-miami-beach/images/wibEoJm4KXyb/1120x700/sucp97bagxtwmum9lvmg.jpg)\
\
Art Fair\
\
Art Basel Miami Beach\
\
03 Dec 2025 — 07 Dec 2025\
\
Miami Beach Convention Center\
\
Miami Beach, United States](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/art-basel-miami-beach-miami-beach)

### Basel Highlights from New York

[Berry Campbell](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/berry-campbell)
A focused, museum level presentation of women abstractionists who shaped mid century American art.

[Leon Tovar Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/leon-tovar-gallery)
A thoughtful selection of Latin American modernists who blend experimentation and political consciousness.

[Sikkema Jenkins and Company](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/sikkema-jenkins-co)
A mix of contemporary practices that bring together craft, identity, and conceptual clarity.

[Candice Madey in Nova](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/candice-madey)
A beautifully intimate presentation that merges materiality and queer sensibility.

Why collectors love Basel  
It helps you understand what museums will care about next year. It is also the best place to see artists whose markets have strong foundations and solid historical grounding.

[NADA Miami](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025)
 - The fair where discovery and experimentation take the lead
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

NADA is the fair that artists, curators, and young collectors talk about the most. It is energetic. It is experiment friendly. It is where new conversations begin.

NADA has roots in the New York emerging scene. Many of the participating galleries are from the Lower East Side, Chinatown, Tribeca, and Brooklyn.These spaces often discover artists before larger galleries do, and they follow their instincts rather than the market.

If Basel is about clarity, NADA is about possibility. It is the place to spot artists who will matter in a year or two.

### [NADA Highlights from New York](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025)

[Tara Downs](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/tara-downs)
A gallery known for conceptual sharpness and artists who push the edges of form. A great stop for collectors seeking intellectually bold work.

[Asya Geisberg Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/asya-geisberg-gallery)
Cosmopolitan and emotionally rich. Many of their artists bridge cultural traditions and contemporary experimentation.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/harkawik-new-york)

[EUROPA](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/europa-nyc)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/harkawik-new-york)

Milly Skellington’s presentation fractures the hyper-saturated image world into trembling fields of color, turning watches, memorials, and language into kaleidoscopic portraits of a digital age where reality splinters faster than we can grasp it.

[The Locker Room](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/the-locker-room)
Young, lively, community driven, and full of energy. Wonderful for collectors who want to support the next generation directly.

Why collectors love NADA  
You can build relationships early. You can buy work at a moment of real growth. And you can see where the ideas that will influence future exhibitions are coming from.

[![NADA Miami 2025](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025/images/fKAnMSoIrPp0/1120x1400/541583198-18524867881001589-5240681448274213647-n.jpg)\
\
Art Fair\
\
NADA Miami 2025\
\
02 Dec 2025 — 06 Dec 2025\
\
Ice Palace Studios\
\
Miami, United States](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025)

*   I've seen this
*   [Comment on NADA Miami 2025](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/nada-miami-2025#conversation)
    
*       Share NADA Miami 2025 with your friends
    

[Untitled Art Miami](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/untitled-art-miami-beach)
 - The fair for beautifully curated, material forward, cross disciplinary work
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Untitled has a very different feeling from both Basel and NADA. It is open, spacious, and designed with a curator’s eye. Each booth feels intentional. This is the fair where materials really speak and where artists push the boundaries of process.

New York galleries at Untitled present work that blends photography, sculpture, digital media, installation, textile, and conceptual research. It is an excellent fair for collectors who want to understand the technical and emotional intelligence behind contemporary practice.

[![Untitled Art Miami Beach](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/untitled-art-miami-beach/images/AsI6Z6wudpn6/1120x746/c05ac0d1bfca5450367e0ac69f03a623695be00a-8256x5504.jpg)\
\
Art Fair\
\
Untitled Art Miami Beach\
\
03 Dec 2025 — 07 Dec 2025\
\
Miami, United States](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/untitled-art-miami-beach)

*   Save / follow
*   I've seen this
*   [Comment on Untitled Art Miami Beach](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/untitled-art-miami-beach#conversation)
    
*       Share Untitled Art Miami Beach with your friends
    

### Untitled Highlights from New York

[bitforms gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/bitforms-gallery)
A leader in digital and technology centered art.

[Yossi Milo Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/yossi-milo-gallery)
Photography that moves beyond photography. Sculptural processes, tactile surfaces, and conceptual depth.

[Fridman Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/fridman-gallery)
Fridman Gallery presents new works by Nate Lewis, Remy Jungerman, and Naomi Lisiki, alongside Dindga McCannon’s pioneering mixed-media quilts, offering a booth that bridges representation and abstraction through innovative techniques and organic patterning.

[Alyssa Davis Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/alyssa-davis-gallery)
Small but incredibly focused. Concept driven work with a strong intellectual foundation.

Why collectors love Untitled  
It is the best place to understand how artists are experimenting with materials. It is also the most relaxed fair, which makes it easier for new collectors to slow down and fall in love with the work in front of them.

How to Choose Your Fair in Miami
--------------------------------

Each fair serves a different purpose for new collectors.

Choose Basel if you want to learn which artists have strong historical foundations and who museums are talking about.

Choose NADA if you want to discover emerging artists and support galleries that shape the next generation.  
Choose Untitled if you want to explore cross disciplinary, material forward work in a beautifully curated environment.

Together, the fairs offer a full map of contemporary art. New York’s presence helps clarify that map. Whether you are just beginning your collection or looking to deepen it, Miami Art Week is the perfect place to explore what New York galleries are championing next.

, [Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/artrabbit/)
, [LinkedIn](https://uk.linkedin.com/company/artrabbit-ltd)
 and [Pinterest](https://www.pinterest.co.uk/artrabbit/)
.

# Roundups, reviews, recommendations from the ArtRabbit Team

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

  [![Wax, Relax, Reflect: Jason Shulman Turns a Hackney Salon into a Sanctuary](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/wax-relax-reflect-jason-shulman-turns-a-hackney-salon-into-a-sanctuary/images/iIpdTCjoz2ZX/300x168/0,160/1700x956/Wax-and-Relax-Press-release-pic-1-1.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/wax-relax-reflect-jason-shulman-turns-a-hackney-salon-into-a-sanctuary)

11 Nov 2025

London

[Wax, Relax, Reflect: Jason Shulman Turns a Hackney Salon into a Sanctuary\
-------------------------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/wax-relax-reflect-jason-shulman-turns-a-hackney-salon-into-a-sanctuary)

A pop-up show in a former East London salon offers quiet revelation: Jason Shulman’s Wax & Relax reduces spectacle to one flame and transforms it into an experience that feels both intimate and infinite.

  [![Installation view, Spotlight on David Gilbert at Chris Sharp Gallery, Los Angeles, 2025. Courtesy of the artist and Chris Sharp Gallery.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/untitled/images/UY3YmuXk2IVt/300x168/0,142/2778x1563/Spotlight-on-David-Gilbert-at-Chris-Sharp-Gallery.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/spotlight-on-david-gilbert-at-chris-sharp-gallery)

10 Nov 2025

Los Angeles

[Spotlight on David Gilbert at Chris Sharp Gallery\
-------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/november/spotlight-on-david-gilbert-at-chris-sharp-gallery)

David Gilbert transforms hand-built paper castles into dreamlike scenes that blur fantasy and reality. His photographs explore queerness, fragility and transformation within the walls of imagined sanctuaries.

  [![Seasons Change: Now the Real Exhibitions Begin, Exhibition hightlights for this coming week in New York City](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/seasons-change-now-the-real-exhibitions-begin/images/HjfBKDQWSm4M/300x168/0,187/2000x1125/Charisse-Pearlina-Weston-mis-me-squeeze-1.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/seasons-change-now-the-real-exhibitions-begin)

29 Oct 2025

New York

[Seasons Change: Now the Real Exhibitions Begin\
----------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/seasons-change-now-the-real-exhibitions-begin)

November in New York invites deeper looking. Step into the city’s most resonant exhibitions this week, where time slows and art begins to breathe again.

  [![Installation view of Carol Bove: Nights of Cabiria at Gagosian, Beverly Hills. Photo by Maris Hutchinson](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/untitled/images/7pGcqHLkFPWF/300x168/0,364/4800x2700/Carol-Bove-Nights-of-Cabiria-September-25-November-1-2025-Beverly-Hills.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/carol-bove-nights-of-cabiria-at-gagosian)

28 Oct 2025

Los Angeles

[Carol Bove: Nights of Cabiria at Gagosian\
-----------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/carol-bove-nights-of-cabiria-at-gagosian)

Carol Bove has transformed Gagosian Beverly Hills into a striking site-specific installation. Her sculptural frameworks echo the gallery’s architecture, a mesmerising fusion of structure, surface, and cinematic reference.

  [![This Week in NYC: Downtown After Dark, Uptown by Day, Harlem All Weekend](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/this-week-in-nyc-downtown-after-dark-uptown-by-day-harlem-all-weekend/images/TzIIQAWb61lP/300x168/0,179/1700x956/Geumhyumg-Postcard-1.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/this-week-in-nyc-downtown-after-dark-uptown-by-day-harlem-all-weekend)

22 Oct 2025

New York

[This Week in NYC: Downtown After Dark, Uptown by Day, Harlem All Weekend\
------------------------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/this-week-in-nyc-downtown-after-dark-uptown-by-day-harlem-all-weekend)

Downtown glows for Autumn Art Night, Madison Avenue opens its storied galleries, and Harlem’s Stay Frosty transforms a parking lot into a vibrant weekend-long open-air art fair. Morgan Everhart curates this week’s essential NYC art picks.

  [![Alfonso Gonzalez Jr., NO PARKING, Matthew Brown, Los Angeles, 2025. Installation view. (Photo: Paul Salveson)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/untitled/images/LMBcQHeUjVmM/300x168/0,146/2817x1585/Alfonso-Gonzalez-Jr-NO-PARKING-Matthew-Brown-Los-Angeles-2025-Installation-view-Photo-Paul-Salveson.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/alfonso-gonzalez-jr-no-parking-at-matthew-brown-gallery)

21 Oct 2025

Los Angeles

[Alfonso Gonzalez Jr.: No Parking at Matthew Brown Gallery\
---------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/alfonso-gonzalez-jr-no-parking-at-matthew-brown-gallery)

In No Parking, Alfonso Gonzalez Jr. turns Los Angeles’s parked, burned, and abandoned cars into haunting portraits of urban life, revealing human stories through rust, paint, and time.

  [![Mirror States: An Intimate Art & Wine Tour Through Tribeca and the LES](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/mirror-states-an-intimate-art-wine-tour-through-tribeca-and-the-les/images/Is5sFAb6ecPf/300x168/0,159/1700x956/Installation-view-Hank-Willis-Thomas-I-AM-MANY-2025-Jack-Shainman-Gallery-46-Lafayette-Street-New-York-NY-Hank-Willis-Thomas-Courtesy-of-the-artist-and-Jack-Shainman-Gallery-New-York-Photo-Dan-Bradica-Studio-1.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/mirror-states-an-intimate-art-wine-tour-through-tribeca-and-the-les)

15 Oct 2025

New York

[Mirror States: An Intimate Art & Wine Tour Through Tribeca and the LES\
----------------------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/mirror-states-an-intimate-art-wine-tour-through-tribeca-and-the-les)

Last chance to book! Join ArtRabbit’s Mirror States tour on October 18 for an afternoon of art, wine, and conversation across Tribeca and the LES. Meet gallery directors and explore works by Vladislav Markov, Márton Nemes, and Hank Willis Thomas.

  [![Beyond Frieze Week: London’s Best Exhibitions and Art Experiences This October](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/beyond-frieze-week-londons-best-exhibitions-and-art-experiences-this-october/images/RXDflSdeA7O4/300x168/0,539/4269x2401/04-ESTELLEHANANIA.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/beyond-frieze-week-londons-best-exhibitions-and-art-experiences-this-october)

14 Oct 2025

London

[Beyond Frieze Week: London’s Best Exhibitions and Art Experiences This October\
------------------------------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/october/beyond-frieze-week-londons-best-exhibitions-and-art-experiences-this-october)

From shimmering paint skins to nocturnal light shows, our guide to the best exhibitions and art experiences beyond the fair this Frieze Week London.

Online
------

[Hosted by: West Dean | London](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/west-dean-london)

InstructionsToggle Instructions

Registrants will be sent a Microsoft Teams link prior to the event.

*   Language: English
*   [Join the event](https://www.westdean.ac.uk/open-days/vod-interior-design)
    

Virtual Open Day - Interior Design

### About

Unable to attend our Campus Open Day? Join us for a live, online Open Day session to hear more about our [courses in Interior Design](https://www.westdean.ac.uk/open-days/vod-interior-design#courses)
, student life, funding your studies, admissions and application advice. 

Date: Thursday 8 January 2026  
Time: 6-8pm

Registrants will be sent a Microsoft Teams link prior to the event. 

[Book your place](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/virtual-open-day-interior-design-2026/cta?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.westdean.ac.uk%2Fopen-days%2Fvod-interior-design&s=w)

#### What to expect? Toggle

*   [Design / Fashion](https://www.artrabbit.com/disciplines/design-fashion)

# Curator in Residence: SAC International Curatorial Residency Program 2026

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

SAC International Curatorial Residency Program 2026 is the residency program at Barcelona's Sant Andreu Contemporani, in collaboration with Fabra i Coats - Fàbrica de Creació de Barcelona, available to international curators.

**Who can apply:** As part of the program, we are announcing an open call for proposals to choose an international curator who will be part of the Miquel Casablancas Prize for the Visual Arts’ jury in 2026, and will later develop a curatorial project with a selection of catalan artists chosen from applicants to the prize. The project must be presented at the country of residence of the curator or in another international venue that accepts it.

**What you get:** The residency covers the expenses of jurying the prize and for the curatorial proposal (2,000 € subject to applicable taxes), the management and production costs of the exhibition (2,000 € subject to applicable taxes), accommodation and travel.

**Deadline 02 January 2026**

Organiser: Sant Andreu Contemporani

Locations: Europe

[Apply](https://santandreucontemporani.org/es/convocatorias-es/open-call-sac-international-curatorial-residency-program-2026-2/)

Back to all [artist opportunties](https://www.artrabbit.com/artist-opportunities)

# Artist in Residence: QE Artists-in-Residence

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

A funded four-month residency opportunity for emerging and mid-career artists working across all disciplines in London. We invite you to apply and encourage you to share this opportunity with fellow artists in your community.

**Who can apply:** We're looking for two visual artists working with a distinct and compelling voice who demonstrates clear mastery of their chosen media. Our selection committee is particularly interested in providing opportunity and a platform to underrepresented artists in the early or middle stages of their careers.

**What you get:** The residency offers £3,000 per month over four months (£12,000 total), plus an allowance of up to £1,000 for art materials. At the conclusion of the residency, we'll mount an exhibition of the work created, and at least one piece will be incorporated into our permanent collection.

**Deadline 06 January 2026**

Organiser: Quinn Emanuel Arts Foundation

Locations: United Kingdom

[Apply](https://www.quinnemanuel.com/artists-in-residence/our-participating-offices/london-uk)

Back to all [artist opportunties](https://www.artrabbit.com/artist-opportunities)

---

# Concrete Poetry: Why Swansea Should Be Your Next Arts and Culture Travel Destination 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

*     [![Swansea Marina. Photo by Avi Varma. Copyright the photographer](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/september/concrete-poetry-why-swansea-should-be-your-next-arts-and-culture-travel-destination/image/images/N41ecl06r8W8/460x460/0,0/3024x3024/marina-swansea-avi-varma.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/september/concrete-poetry-why-swansea-should-be-your-next-arts-and-culture-travel-destination/image/images/Lv1H0wwy32NM/920x920/0,0/3024x3024/marina-swansea-avi-varma.jpg)
    
    Swansea Marina. Photo by Avi Varma. Copyright the photographer.
    
*     [![Glynn Vivian, Swansea. Photo by Chris Boorman. Courtesy of Glynn Vivian.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/september/concrete-poetry-why-swansea-should-be-your-next-arts-and-culture-travel-destination/image/images/KWYBR6Na1WFN/689x460/0,0/1649x1100/glynn-vivian-photo-by-chris-boorman-copy.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/september/concrete-poetry-why-swansea-should-be-your-next-arts-and-culture-travel-destination/image/images/toxCvUwyy6ck/1379x920/0,0/1649x1100/glynn-vivian-photo-by-chris-boorman-copy.jpg)
    
    Glynn Vivian, Swansea. Photo by Chris Boorman. Courtesy of Glynn Vivian.
    

With an abundance of industrial history and Modernist architecture setting the scene, we take a tour of Swansea’s must-see museums, galleries, and project spaces.

Following in the footsteps of Dylan Thomas, and inspired by a thriving artist-led scene and dynamic museum programming, we couldn’t agree more with the poet’s assertion that ‘Swansea is a town where art is alive’. ArtRabbit visited [Swansea](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-kingdom/swansea)
 on a brisk September day, keen to explore contemporary art, culture, and history in Wales’s second largest city. With the journey just under [3 hours direct from London Paddington with Great Western Railway](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)
, yet feeling further flung than many other major UK cities, consider Swansea your next cultural weekend destination.

Like [Plymouth, which we visited earlier this year](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/may/next-stop-plymouth-contemporary-art-iconic-public-sculpture-in-britains-ocean-city)
, [Swansea](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-kingdom/swansea)
 is a large port city bearing all the typical markers: grand Victorian institutional buildings, industrial sprawl, and post-war civic planning make for a visually arresting tour through the city, before you even encounter any of the top-tier art and culture. Once boasting numerous docks, it was an important centre for many trades including coal, tin and copper, mined from all over the South Wales valleys. Heavily bombed during the Second World War, it has undergone waves of regeneration throughout the decades, leading to a palimpsestic urban landscape which has no doubt inspired the city’s numerous resident artists and artists-in-residence.

City Centre
-----------

Upon stepping out of Swansea station, you’ll spot three words inlaid in the paving: ‘AMBITION IS CRITICAL’. Commissioned by Swansea City Council in 1993, this is a poem by poet David Hughes, part of a series. This motivating line somehow encompasses a mood to the city’s cultural scene, which produces a huge breadth relative to its population of 250k.

This summer, Swansea’s major art gallery and museum, [Glynn Vivian](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/glynn-vivian-art-gallery)
, opened [Out of this World](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world)
, a major new exhibition by artist [Heather Phillipson](https://www.artrabbit.com/people/heather-phillipson/artist)
. Following our visit, we spoke to Heather about her work and the research presented at the museum, drawn from the [Imperial War Museum](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/imperial-war-museum)
 archive and [Cyfarthfa Castle](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/cyfarthfa-castle-museum-and-art-gallery)
, in an exclusive piece, to be published later this month.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world)
[![Heather Phillipson: Out of this World](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world/images/NSD7ykT6fOS2/1120x746/20240711-GlynnVivian-HeatherPhillipson-003.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
Heather Phillipson: Out of this World\
\
12 Jul 2024 — 26 Jan 2025\
\
Glynn Vivian Art Gallery\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/heather-phillipson-out-of-this-world)

*   Save / follow
*   I've seen this

*       Share Heather Phillipson: Out of this World with your friends
    

A few minutes walk from Glynn Vivian, [Elysium Gallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/elysium-gallery-bar-venue)
 is an artists’ studio complex with a bar and gallery open to the public. The gallery itself is extensive, and presents a high-quality programme from artists both local, national and international. Opening to coincide with [Swansea Arts Weekend](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/swansea-arts-weekend)
, and programmed in partnership with [Ffotogallery](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/ffotogallery)
, [The Imagined Land of Belonging](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging)
 will exhibit work by Latin American and Caribbean Female photographers.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging)
[![The imagined land of belonging](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging/images/XLXd0qcpWWwT/1120x1600/Julieta-Anaut-Simulations-of-an-unknown-nostalgia-Wishes-are-Roots-2018-2021.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
The imagined land of belonging\
\
04 Oct 2024 — 26 Oct 2024\
\
elysium gallery | bar | venue\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging)

*   Save / follow
*   I've seen this
*   [Comment on The imagined land of belonging](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/the-imagined-land-of-belonging#conversation)
    
*       Share The imagined land of belonging with your friends
    

Elysium isn’t the city’s only artists’ studio and gallery. Not surprisingly, considering [UWTSD: Swansea College of Art](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/swansea-college-of-art-uwtsd)
 is renowned as one of the best places in the UK to study art, it’s evident that the city retains and nurtures creative talent.

Neighbouring Elysium, [GS Artists](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/gs-artists)
 is a not-for-profit project space founded by artist Jane Simpson seven years ago, and is now run by a group of freelance artists. It aims to offer a ‘place to connect, build links and develop the Swansea art community’. This month, exhibitions have included [ILLUMINATE](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light)
, an exhibition of photographic work which highlights modernist architecture in Swansea, among other cities.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light)
[![ILLUMINATE: Architecture and Light](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light/images/onetpBjug6E4/1120x750/rob-lycett-huddersfield-3.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
ILLUMINATE: Architecture and Light\
\
12 Sep 2024 — 28 Sep 2024\
\
GS Artists\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/illuminate-architecture-and-light)

*   Save / follow

*       Share ILLUMINATE: Architecture and Light with your friends
    

Also worth a visit is [Volcano](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/volcano)
. Set on the ground floor of Elysium’s studio building, in a former department store, it is primarily a performance space but also hosts exhibitions, community groups, fairs and exhibitions, all with a DIY aesthetic.

Maritime Quarter
----------------

The walk from the city centre to the Maritime Quarter is mostly pedestrianised, making for a pleasant 10 to 15-minute stroll. Now would be a good time to pull out a copy of Swansea Modernist, published by [The Modernist](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/the-modernist)
, and make a note of the city’s architectural highlights from the post-war period. A stop at Kardomah Cafe, perfectly preserved since the 1960s, offers up another public art commission in poem form: [Michelangelo, Ping-Pong, Ambition, Sibelius, and Girls…](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls)
 by DJ Roberts, a subtle neon in homage to the city’s most famous creative, poet Dylan Thomas.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls)
[![Michelangelo, Ping-Pong, Ambition, Sibelius, and Girls…](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls/images/AQZxPetydE5F/1120x747/michelangelo-ping-pong-dj-roberts-day.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
Michelangelo, Ping-Pong, Ambition, Sibelius, and Girls…\
\
01 Sep 2015 — 31 Oct 2030\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/michelangelo-pingpong-ambition-sibelius-and-girls)

*       Share Michelangelo, Ping-Pong, Ambition, Sibelius, and Girls… with your friends
    

Once down at the Maritime Quarter, you can learn more about Thomas at the [Dylan Thomas Centre](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/dylan-thomas-centre)
. The permanent exhibition [Love The Words](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/love-the-words)
 features interactive displays, recordings, and objects which give insight into the great poet’s life and work.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/love-the-words)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/love-the-words)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/love-the-words)

Dylan Thomas Centre\

Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/love-the-words)

*       Share Love the Words with your friends
    

From here, continue your museum tour at [Swansea Museum](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/swansea-museum)
. Here, a small exhibition titled [Remembering the Cockle Women](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women)
 includes loans of photographs, prints, and paintings from the descendants of the Welsh cockle industry’s long-established families, alongside a film work. For a 360-degree, enhanced experience, make a visit to Swansea Indoor Market. One of the UK’s largest working market halls, and, as it happens, another of the city’s modernist icons, to pick up a punnet of cockles with vinegar, still locally picked, for a few pounds. The exhibition closes this weekend, but the dish remains perennially popular.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women)

\
Exhibition\
\
Remembering the Cockle Women\
\
23 Mar 2024 — 30 Sep 2024\
\
Swansea Museum\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women)

*   Save / follow 1

*   [Comment on Remembering the Cockle Women](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/remembering-the-cockle-women#conversation)
    
*       Share Remembering the Cockle Women with your friends
    

There are multiple exhibits on at the [National Waterfront Museum](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/national-waterfront-museum)
, which is dedicated to industrial heritage. This is a broad remit, and its 15 themed galleries include large scale industrial machinery used in the coal and tin industries, alongside maritime equipment and social artefacts. Opened this year, [Ours to Tell](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/ours-to-tell-national-waterfront-museum)
 presents works newly acquired by the museum, selected by members of the city’s LGBTQ+ community. It’s a small but moving exhibit. Highlights include a pack of love hearts spelling out a marriage proposal and a ‘Gay News Fights On’ badge from the 1977 Whitehouse v. Lemon trial.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/ours-to-tell-national-waterfront-museum)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/ours-to-tell-national-waterfront-museum)

[![Ours to Tell](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/ours-to-tell-national-waterfront-museum/images/dM1Re1mfH9gB/1120x938/national-waterfront-museum-ours-to-tell.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
Ours to Tell\
\
16 Mar 2024 — 21 Jan 2025\
\
National Waterfront Museum\
\
Swansea, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/ours-to-tell-national-waterfront-museum)

*       Share Ours to Tell with your friends
    

Whilst the museums are a major attraction of the Maritime Quarter, don’t neglect to visit the small but ambitious Mission Gallery. Based in a former seamen’s church, the gallery presents a programme of contemporary visual arts and craft. Upcoming exhibition [We Are All Artists](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/we-are-all-artists)
 will show work by renowned Welsh ceramicist [Lowri Davies](https://www.artrabbit.com/people/lowri-davies/artist)
 alongside members of the Chinese in Wales Association.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/we-are-all-artists)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/we-are-all-artists)

Swansea Arts Weekend
--------------------

From Friday, 4 to Saturday, 6 October, [Swansea Arts Weekend](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/swansea-arts-weekend)
 will be presenting exhibitions, workshops, and performances across the city with partner organisations. Alongside the exhibitions noted above, you can discover events such as [Night of the Triangles](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/night-of-the-triangles)
 at [GS Artists](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/gs-artists)
; [Ffiesta am Byth](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/ffiesta-am-byth)
 at [Volcano](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/volcano)
 and a [skate photography workshop](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/skate-photography-workshop)
 in conjunction with the [Skin Phillips: 360°](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/skin-phillips-360)
 exhibition at [Glynn Vivian](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/glynn-vivian-art-gallery)
.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/swansea-arts-weekend)

Travel with a Long Weekender ticket
-----------------------------------

Great Western Railway’s Long Weekender tickets offer fully flexible travel at 50% the price of an Anytime Return. Travel on a Friday or Saturday and return on a Monday to take advantage. [Book your tickets here](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)
.

→ The South West Art Travel Companion: [A GWR-Partnered Guide to Exploring the South West, West, and South Wales](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Thanks to our partnership with [GWR](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)
, this guide brings the art-filled landscapes of the South West, West, and South Wales to your doorstep. Travel from one art exhibition to another, discovering how art transforms within the context of its environment. Embrace the convenience of [booking ahead and travelling during quieter times with GWR Railcards](https://bit.ly/43YY2Wf)
, tailored for explorers young and seasoned. [Plan your journey here](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)
.

# Artist in Residence: Makers Residency - 3 Months Free Space

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

We are offering a creative practitioner living in Waltham Forest the opportunity to grow their skills and practice. This includes access to our shared studios, free use of our wood and metal workshops, guidance, and skill development with our specialist technicians.

**Who can apply:**

*   Waltham Forest resident
*   A creative practitioner / artist / maker with a strong interest in wood and/or metalwork.
*   A practitioner who values community-driven spaces and believes in the power of making to create positive change" Local to Waltham Forest, interested in woodwork or metalwork, from a background underrepresented in the arts.

**What you get:**

*   Free desk space in our shared makers’ studio for 3 months
*   Free access to our wood and metal machine shops and benches
*   Free workshop induction (wood machine shop, metalwork, forge, lathes) - - Opportunities to develop teaching skills
*   Opportunities to get involved in our young people and community outreach programme

**Deadline 04 January 2026**

Organiser: Blackhorse Workshop CIC

Locations: United Kingdom

[Apply](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLScU8UWTo6m7KP7pPzVqvzxgBzdTpkS9rIDVNr79ogxOV_uzEQ/viewform)

Back to all [artist opportunties](https://www.artrabbit.com/artist-opportunities)

#### Artist opportunities closing soon

# For Organisations 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

You’ve nurtured artists and curators, and have made a home for creatives and their corresponding exhibitions. Now it’s time to get the word out and get audiences in. That’s what we’re here for. With ArtRabbit, you’ll be amazed by the amount of organic traffic your events can generate.

Organisation Checklist
----------------------

Organisations on ArtRabbit include art organisations of any scale, galleries, project spaces, artist-run spaces, cultural organisations and educational organisations. If you’re one of the above, make the most of ArtRabbit and be sure to do all of the following:

**Sign up for an account ✔️**

[Sign up here](https://www.artrabbit.com/register)
, or find out more [about us here](https://www.artrabbit.com/about-artrabbit/about)
.

**Read our Community Guidelines ✔️**

Our [Community Guidelines](https://www.artrabbit.com/about-artrabbit/community-guidelines)
 are an important code of conduct for maintaining a safe, useful and welcoming platform for all.

**List or claim your organisation ✔️**

Use the search bar to find your organisation on ArtRabbit. If it exists, go to its dedicated organisation page and click on the ‘claim’ button, then follow the prompts.

If your organisation or venue is not yet on ArtRabbit, [you can list the venue here](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/add-organisation)
.

**Verify your organisation page **✔️****

If you're creating your organisation page, be sure to tick "Yes" under the questions "Are you the owner or administrator of the venue?"  
If your organisation has already been added, you'll need to claim it to verify it.

Make sure you're logged into ArtRabbit using an email address associated with your organisation, then simply navigate to your organisation page, click "Claim - Claim this organisation", fill in the short form and click "Next".

After this is complete, we'll verify your organisation so that it'll get a snazzy green check badge on its page, a feature that will make it more popular among our users.

**List your events ✔️**

Have an event coming up? [List the event here](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/find-venue)
, or navigate to your dedicated organisation page on ArtRabbit and click on the “add event” button. By adding an event from your organisation page, the location details will be pre-filled.

If your event is taking place in London, the UK, Berlin, or New York, (more locations to come!) we’ll include them in our weekly location-specific newsletters. Every listed exhibition is considered, no matter how small, so make sure your events and exhibitions are on the ArtRabbit platform.

**List your festival, biennale or art week **✔️****

Organising a festival, biennial, art week or any other type of umbrella event that's taking place across several venues? Here's how to can use ArtRabbit to your advantage: First, list your main event with as much information as possible. Then, list all related events at their respective art venues. You'll see an option to "Add related event" for each event you add. Start typing in the name of your main event, then select your main event from the dropdown and confirm the relation by clicking the "Relate" button. We'll take care of the rest.

Want this feature to work even harder for your event? We can create a branded web and app feature for your entire events programme with custom branding and optimised map functionality. Get a quote now by contacting us at [support@artrabbit.com](mailto:support@artrabbit.com)
.

**Add online events ✔️**

You can add online events either from an organisation page or from "Add an Event" in the main menu.

To add online events from an organisation, select "Online", then fill out the details as you would normally. To add online events from the main menu, select "Online", then either continue as the host or find the organisation that is hosting the event. If the organisation doesn't appear in the dropdown, you can add the new organisation to ArtRabbit, then create the online event. Fill out the details as you would normally, and publish the event. Be sure to add instructions on how to join the event, even if it's simply opening up a website.

**Boost your events **✔️****

Looking to get more traffic through your doors and more buzz about your events? You can now boost your events to get them listed on our city-specific featured list of exhibitions and events.

**Add calls to action **✔️****

If you’re looking to direct audiences to a website where you sell tickets, memberships, books, prints etc, or even if you’re not selling anything, you can add up to three Calls-to-Action on your event page to prompt page visitors to click through to your site.

**Link to and promote your ArtRabbit profile with our logos and badges **✔️****

To help you link to and promote your ArtRabbit profile, we have created badges you can add to your website, online portfolio, or newsletters. Don’t underestimate the influence you have over your own network: by directing more traffic to your ArtRabbit profile, you’ll be able to reap the benefits of our targeted emails as well as the [upcoming and suggested events](https://www.artrabbit.com/support/suggested-and-upcoming-events)
 function. [More information on ArtRabbit logos and badges here](https://www.artrabbit.com/support/logo-and-badges)
.

**Subscribe to our newsletters **✔️****

Newsletters go out every Wednesday and cover new exhibitions and events for eight consecutive days. Find out what’s happening at other venues and galleries in London, throughout the UK, Berlin or New York and be in the know. [You can subscribe to our newsletters here](https://www.artrabbit.com/subscribe)
.

**Download the App **✔️****

The ArtRabbit App is the best way to discover art exhibitions near you, find out what’s the most popular shows in your city and keep track of your own cultural exposure. With an interactive map and the ability to save events you’re interested in, it’s the perfect app to help you uncover the cultural riches around you.

We also publish featured lists on the App every season, so be sure to add your events to be considered for this spot.

Download the ArtRabbit app for [iPhone](https://itunes.apple.com/gb/app/artrabbit/id1144550147?mt=8)
 or [Android](https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.artrabbit.arnativeapp)
.

**Connect with us on Social Media **✔️****

Connect with us on social media for art news, industry insights, art travel suggestions, updates on new services and features, and more. This is ArtRabbit on [Twitter](https://twitter.com/ArtRabbit)
, [Facebook](https://www.facebook.com/ArtRabbit/)
, [Instagram](https://www.instagram.com/artrabbit/)
, [Pinterest](https://www.pinterest.co.uk/artrabbit/)
, and [LinkedIn](https://www.linkedin.com/company/1942389/)
. (Top tip: we love retweeting your events from ArtRabbit!)

**Submit your ArtOpps **✔️****

Our [Artist Opportunity](https://www.artrabbit.com/artist-opportunities)
 board reaches about 5000 unique viewers per week and is the best way to get the quality submissions you’re after. If you’re looking to publish your open call, [fill out this form](http://artrabb.it/1Kul7Vs)
 to be considered.

[Join ArtRabbit's Professional Plans](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/plans)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Showcase artworks for sales, and unlock specialised features to promote your programmes and events.

  ![ArtRabbit for Business](https://img.artrabbit.com/what-you-can-do/organisations/image/images/PljO1b5aI75A/300x178/0,0/1616x960/ArtForBusiness1616x960.jpg)

Questions? Concerns?
--------------------

Still got questions or comments? Then drop us a line at [support@artrabbit.com](mailto:support@artrabbit.com)
.

[![Follow us on ArtRabbit](https://www.artrabbit.com/logos/badge/artrabbit-square-blue.svg)Last reviewed by Vivi on 20 July 2023](https://www.artrabbit.com/people/vivikallinikou)

# Join the ArtRabbit Artist Directory 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

Are you a professional artist looking to expand your horizons with new work, commissions, or placements? The ArtRabbit Artist Directory is your gateway to exciting opportunities in the cultural and commercial spaces. Whether it's projects, commissions, exhibitions, or collections, we use the data submitted to ArtRabbit to identify the perfect artistic collaborations and recommend you for suitable roles.

What is the ArtRabbit Artist Directory?
---------------------------------------

The ArtRabbit Artist Directory is a curated database of professional artists open for work, commissions, and placements. We consult on a wide range of cultural and commercial projects, facilitating the right artistic collaborations across various industries.

Who can join the ArtRabbit Artist Directory?
--------------------------------------------

This service is available exclusively for professional tier account holders on ArtRabbit. If you're an artist looking to expand your professional network and gain access to unique opportunities, this is for you.

How does it work?
-----------------

Once you've filled out the artist questionnaire and updated your profile with your exhibition history and artworks, we use this information to recommend you for relevant projects. Our clients and partners access this pool of talent when they need artists for their projects, ranging from private commissions to public exhibitions.

Is the service currently available?
-----------------------------------

The service is in trial mode at the moment, which means we are still testing and refining how it works. However, you can start taking advantage of the directory right now. Upcoming collaborations include {{ insert here }} and have available for launch.

How can I get considered for projects?
--------------------------------------

To be considered:

1.  Upgrade to one of our professional tier plans.
2.  Update your profile and ensure all information is current.
3.  Upload your exhibition history. If there are exhibitions you’ve participated in that are listed on ArtRabbit but you aren’t mentioned as a participating artist, contact our support team for verification and inclusion.
4.  Fill out the artist questionnaire to complete your profile.

How will I know about upcoming opportunities?
---------------------------------------------

If you qualify for any current projects based on the information you've provided, you'll be contacted directly by our team. Selection for projects is based on the specific needs of our partners and clients, who will reach out through us to engage you for their campaigns.

Are these opportunities paid?
-----------------------------

Yes! This service is designed to create an income stream for artists, beyond simply selling artworks. In some cases, we might be able to negotiate a fee for you; in other cases, you’ll be asked to take over the negotiations. However, we will exclusively offer only paid opportunities here.

Are these opportunities location specific?
------------------------------------------

Yes, at the moment in our pilot phase, these projects will focus on the UK market. However, we have plans to expand and partner with international clients and partners very soon.

Will you make this directory publicly available?
------------------------------------------------

Not during our pilot phase. While we're learning how artists plan to make use of it, we prefer to keep it non-public. In the future, if it proves advantageous for artists and partners, we may consider making it publicly accessible. However, this would not be done without providing artists with the opportunity to opt out of being promoted in this manner.

---

04 Sep 2025

[Reframe & Resist: Decolonise Here and Now!\
------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/september/reframe-resist-decolonise-here-and-now-at-harta-space)

Reframe & Resist: Decolonise Here and Now! is an exhibition and public seminar in Kuala Lumpur that asks what it means to live with the word “decolonisation” in the present – the project creates space for reflection, dialogue, and experimentation.

  [![How Can Art Spark Environmental Action? Reflections from a Workshop on Environmental Artivism in Kuala Lumpur](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/june/untitled1/images/r5xdVNrYqHo8/300x168/0,378/4032x2268/Artivism-Imagining-Futures-of-Anthropocene-forum.jpg)](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/june/how-can-art-spark-environmental-action-reflections-from-a-workshop-on-environmental-artivism-in-kuala-lumpur)

11 Jun 2025

[How Can Art Spark Environmental Action? Reflections from a Workshop on Environmental Artivism in Kuala Lumpur\
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------](https://www.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/june/how-can-art-spark-environmental-action-reflections-from-a-workshop-on-environmental-artivism-in-kuala-lumpur)

Artist, curator and ArtRabbit correspondent Jakob van Klang hosted a two-day workshop at British Council Malaysia, exploring how art can spark environmental action through UK and Malaysian collaboration. Here are their reflections.

# Exhibition Opportunity: Altura Credit Union Community Gallery – Exhibition Proposals (Spring 2026)

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

The Cheech invites exhibition proposals for the Altura Credit Union Community Gallery, supporting emerging and mid-career artists and curators with roots in the Inland Empire. Selected proposals will be professionally produced and presented at the museum.

**Who can apply:**  
Artists and/or curators with roots in the Inland Empire region. Open to emerging and mid-career practitioners proposing single-artist or group exhibitions.

**What you get:**  
Exhibition at The Cheech with curatorial fee ($1,000 per half gallery / $2,000 full gallery), professional installation, marketing support, and an exhibition reception hosted by the museum.

**Deadline 04 January 2026**

Organiser: The Cheech Marin Center for Chicano Art & Culture (Riverside Art Museum)

Locations: North America

[Apply](https://riversideartmuseum.org/call-for-exhibition-proposals-altura-credit-union-community-gallery-at-the-cheech/)

Back to all [artist opportunties](https://www.artrabbit.com/artist-opportunities)

# Explore Exeter: A Comprehensive Guide to Arts, Culture, and History 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

*     [![Royal Albert Memorial Museum & Art Gallery Exeter exterior view. Courtesy RAMM Exeter. Copyright RAMM Exeter](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/june/explore-exeter-a-comprehensive-guide-to-arts-culture-and-history/image/images/Vy9aPTSakAiR/689x460/0,0/3996x2667/ramm-exterior-exeter.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/june/explore-exeter-a-comprehensive-guide-to-arts-culture-and-history/image/images/2HybGNaocU85/1378x920/0,0/3996x2667/ramm-exterior-exeter.jpg)
    
    Royal Albert Memorial Museum & Art Gallery Exeter exterior view. Courtesy RAMM Exeter. Copyright RAMM Exeter.
    
*     [![Royal Albert Memorial Museum & Art Gallery Exeter Mezzanine. Courtesy RAMM Exeter. Copyright RAMM Exeter.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/june/explore-exeter-a-comprehensive-guide-to-arts-culture-and-history/image/images/a6jwLqaoAkp0/689x460/0,0/5610x3744/ramm-mezzanine-exeter.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2024/june/explore-exeter-a-comprehensive-guide-to-arts-culture-and-history/image/images/GCrbLzusoEd6/1378x920/0,0/5610x3744/ramm-mezzanine-exeter.jpg)
    
    Royal Albert Memorial Museum & Art Gallery Exeter Mezzanine. Courtesy RAMM Exeter. Copyright RAMM Exeter.
    

A historic city and major interchange for trains travelling from London onto the South West, Exeter makes an excellent stop-off or base to explore the region for families seeking art, culture and local history.

The next stop on our cultural journey around the South West is [Exeter](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-kingdom/exeter)
. With a new exhibition exploring the history of transport and summer holidays approaching, we’re excited to share family-friendly events and must-see attractions in this vibrant city.

If You Only Do One Thing… [Visit RAMM](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/royal-albert-memorial-museum-art-gallery)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Given an afternoon in Exeter, we’d make sure we spent time at the [Royal Albert Memorial Museum & Art Gallery or RAMM for short](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/royal-albert-memorial-museum-art-gallery)
. The newly launched ['Are we nearly there yet?' exhibition](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/are-we-nearly-there-yet-a-history-of-transport)
 at the museum explores the history of transport through the centuries, featuring bold, family-friendly displays and fascinating objects. People of all ages will find something to love here: from the sled from Captain Scott’s ill-fated 1911-12 expedition to Antarctica, to a 1950s flight jacket, an ornate miniature sedan chair, and, of course, the essential working model railway.

Brilliant family-friendly events accompany the exhibition throughout the holidays. Workshops include motorised LEGO race cars, cardboard aeroplanes, and hot air balloon crafts.

This inspired exhibition doesn’t ignore the environmental impact of heavy industrialisation and motorisation. Instead, it asks visitors of all ages to consider the impact our transport choices can have on the environment and the broader issue of climate change, and to contemplate what the future of transport in Exeter might look like.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/are-we-nearly-there-yet-a-history-of-transport)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/are-we-nearly-there-yet-a-history-of-transport)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/are-we-nearly-there-yet-a-history-of-transport)
[![Are we nearly there yet? A History of Transport](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/are-we-nearly-there-yet-a-history-of-transport/images/L7zEgS156mql/1120x778/Are-we-nearly-there-yet-hero-image-transport-scaled.jpg)\
\

For contemporary art aficionados, [Ashanti Hare](https://www.artrabbit.com/people/ashanti-hare/artist)
's commission '[River that never rests](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/river-that-never-rests-by-artist-ashanti-hare)
' offers a compelling portrayal of The River Exe, which is used metaphorically to explore the interwoven histories and cultures specific to Exeter and its broader connections.

Join the Local Creative Crowd: Arts and Museums in Exeter
---------------------------------------------------------

A short walk from RAMM, [Exeter Phoenix](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/exeter-phoenix-gallery)
 is a multi-arts venue with galleries, a cinema, performance spaces, and a café. It supports local creatives through classes, courses, and rehearsal spaces while offering an excellent public programme. Summer programme highlights suitable for young people or children include [Sculpt-a-Selfie](https://exeterphoenix.org.uk/events/sculpt-a-selfie/)
, [Your Face My Face](https://exeterphoenix.org.uk/events/your-face-my-face/)
, [Experimental Drawing](https://exeterphoenix.org.uk/events/experimental-drawing-all-ages/)
, and [Janet Sainsbury](https://www.artrabbit.com/people/janet-sainsbury/artist)
’s exhibition ‘[The Gift Of Nearness](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness)
’.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness)
[![Janet Sainsbury: The Gift Of Nearness](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness/images/wRIac5HWNDXk/1120x1120/Janet-Sainsbury.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
Janet Sainsbury: The Gift Of Nearness\
\
06 Jul 2024 — 01 Sep 2024\
\
Exeter Phoenix Gallery\
\
Exeter, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness)

*   Save / follow
*   I've seen this 1
*   [Comment on Janet Sainsbury: The Gift Of Nearness](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/janet-sainsbury-the-gift-of-nearness#conversation)
    
*       Share Janet Sainsbury: The Gift Of Nearness with your friends
    

Alongside Exeter Phoenix, a number of other organisations are integral to the city’s small but rich arts scene. Also centrally located, [Positive Light Projects](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/positive-light-projects)
 hosts exhibitions and workshops with a number of partners, including Exeter University and the Pelican Project. Rooted in community engagement and social practice, the programme isn’t strictly for kids but is a friendly place to pop-you head into if you do have children in tow, and there’s an exhibition or event happening.

Working across the city, [Art Work Exeter](https://artworkexeter.org.uk/)
 offers a vision for the town that is abundant in ‘inspirational, experimental and creative processes’. This artist-led organisation works in various public spaces including commercial, historic and civic buildings. They are currently in residence as cultural partners at Customs House, where they will be hosting activities through the summer. If their recent Dumpling Day and Display event is anything to go by, Art Work Exeter’s upcoming programme will continue to embrace themes of cultural exchange and community engagement.

Fusing creativity with ecology, the [ART and ENERGY Collective](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/art-and-energy-collective)
 is an award-winning group of artists, tinkerers, researchers, scientists, and makers based in the South West. They hold events throughout the region, but in August, they will be at [The Transit Shed at Exeter Quay](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/transit-shed-and-piazza-terracina-space)
 offering free, family-friendly creative activities with no booking required.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/summer-at-the-quayside)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/summer-at-the-quayside)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/summer-at-the-quayside)

Bring the Drama: Theatre and Performances Across Exeter
-------------------------------------------------------

With Exeter University running one of the best drama courses in the UK, it’s no wonder that there are an extraordinary number of theatre and performance groups, troupes, and venues in Exeter. If you’re keen to sample the best culture the city has to offer, consider including a live performance or, if you’re feeling brave, a hands-on workshop to your itinerary.

Theatre company [Quirk](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/quirk-theatre)
 makes theatre for all generations. Noted for their beautiful stage design and costumes, and drawing from a range of cultural backgrounds and experiences, whether you’re visiting Exeter with kids or not, we recommend you check for a Quirk production.

Signet Theatre offers productions and workshops, so if you’re looking to try your hand at a little am-dram, check out their programme. For those firmly in the audience camp, there’s folk music, Shakespeare, and experimental theatre happening throughout the summer months.

If you're local or spending all of summer in the area, Theatre Alibi is offering a summer school for children to try their hands at theatre making. The week will culminate in a performance of ‘Alice in Wonderland’ for friends and family.

Finally, spoken word producers Spork will be delivering events throughout the holidays, including their summer special in Rougemont Gardens on 1 August. With poetry, spoken word, and comedy on the agenda, we recommend you bring a picnic basket and soak up the atmosphere.

Explore the Past: Something for the History Cool Kids
-----------------------------------------------------

Settled since ancient times, the Romans began developing the town of Isca, with major battles, sieges, and revolutions shaping it into modern-day Exeter. It’s not undergone major urbanisation, and a ramble around the historic streets provides a rich cultural experience. However, for families interested in learning more, the museums in and around the city give insights into ancient, recent, and modern times.

For older family groups, Tucker’s Hall, situated just off historic Fore Street, was home to The Incorporation of Weavers, Fullers & Shearmen in medieval times. Once a place for society meetings and ceremonies, it’s now open to visitors twice a week and hosts an occasional programme of family-friendly events such as historic dress-up or arts and crafts trails.

For exploration further afield, take a train from Exeter Central along the Exe Estuary to Topsham, and make a visit to [Topsham Museum](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/topsham-museum)
. The museum’s collection includes objects from the Roman occupation, the medieval period, and the more recent maritime history.

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944)

[](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944)
[![Countdown to D-Day, 6 June 1944](https://img.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944/images/f6qAOouhemg2/1120x721/Topsham-Museum.jpg)\
\
Exhibition\
\
Countdown to D-Day, 6 June 1944\
\
17 Jan 2024 — 31 Dec 2024\
\
Topsham Museum\
\
Exeter, United Kingdom](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944)

*   Save / follow
*   I've seen this
*   [Comment on Countdown to D-Day, 6 June 1944](https://www.artrabbit.com/events/countdown-to-dday-6-june-1944#conversation)
    
*       Share Countdown to D-Day, 6 June 1944 with your friends
    

Hop back on the train to the popular resort town [Exmouth](https://www.artrabbit.com/places/united-kingdom/exmouth)
 and you can visit A la Ronde, a curious rotunda house built by two cousins, Jane and Mary, in the 1700s. After years spent travelling the world, collecting ideas and cultural references, at A la Ronde the cousins indulged their passion for design - creating a shell gallery, feather frieze, along with mosaic work, papercuts, and other crafted items.

For more recent history, [Bill Douglas Cinema](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/the-bill-douglas-cinema-museum)
 at Exeter University is home to one of the largest collections of material on the moving image in Britain. Though there are no public events on offer, objects have been put on display with younger visitors in mind - including shadow puppets, early moving toys, and magic lanterns. It is a little outside the centre of Exeter but well worth a visit.

History buffs will find more to explore by returning to [RAMM](https://www.artrabbit.com/organisations/royal-albert-memorial-museum-art-gallery)
, where alongside temporary exhibitions like ‘Are we nearly there yet?’, a vast array of historical collections await. From social history to natural sciences and antiquities, there’s something for everyone to find wonder in. Our highlights include [George Montague’s Molluscs](https://rammcollections.org.uk/collections-stories/george-montagu-molluscs-a-designated-collection/)
 - a vast collection of shells awarded Designated status by Arts Council England, and [Caleb Hedgeland’s model of Exeter](https://rammuseum.org.uk/collections/collection-areas/local-history/)
, constructed between 1827 and 1824. It’s one of the earliest surviving models of any town in Britain and the only record of many buildings and streets which were later demolished.

With culture in all its forms on offer in Exeter, we encourage you to make it your next exploration destination, whether you’re with family, friends, or going solo. [Plan your journey here](https://bit.ly/3U81LO0)
.

Thank you to [Arts and Culture Exeter](https://www.artsandcultureexeter.co.uk/)
 for their insider knowledge, which helped us put this guide together.

# OmVed Gardens: A Living, Breathing Celebration of Food, Ecology, and Culture 

### Keyword search

Find events, people, organisations or locations by name

 

### Location search

Use the [events](https://www.artrabbit.com/events)
 or the [venues](https://www.artrabbit.com/venues)
 search to find listings near a location.

*     [![The Greenhouse at OmVed Gardens – a double-height space designed to maximise passive solar gain and natural ventilation. Photograph © Maurizio Mucciola.](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/june/omved-gardens-a-living-breathing-celebration-of-food-ecology-and-culture/image/images/kGFjvtL6JbVX/689x460/0,0/4994x3333/OmVed-Greenhouse-Maurizio-Mucciola.jpg)](https://img.artrabbit.com/network/features/2025/june/omved-gardens-a-living-breathing-celebration-of-food-ecology-and-culture/image/images/E6MGpN9mWdAb/1378x920/0,0/4994x3333/OmVed-Greenhouse-Maurizio-Mucciola.jpg)
